## Finite-Core A — sampled coefficient non-concentration

### Result

I cannot prove sampled coefficient non-concentration from the current paper-state. The proof needs a new **pointwise arithmetic/sampling separation theorem** for the actual zeta core map

\[
m\mapsto \theta(m)
\]

relative to analytic small-value sets. The attached deployment explicitly identifies this as the Finite-Core A target and states that compactness, finite determinacy, zero-spacing, endpoint-gap controls, and \(N\)-point positivity do not presently imply the needed bound. 

---

# 1. Target theorem

Let

\[
F_N(\theta,Q)
=
c_{\core,2N-1}(\theta)
+
\sum_{j\ge1}
c_{\core,2N-1+2j}(\theta)
h_j(1^2,\dots,N^2)Q^{-2j},
\]

and define the required scale

\[
\Lambda(m,Q)
:=
C_*
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right).
\]

The theorem needed is

\[
\boxed{
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
|F_N(\theta(m),Q)|
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q)
}
\]

for every actual zeta finite-core sample

\[
\theta(m)\notin \mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

This is stronger than finite determinacy. Finite determinacy says some coefficient is nonzero. This theorem says the sampled finite coefficient vector is not too small at the exact \(N\)-point scale.

---

# 2. Zero-spacing and endpoint gaps do not imply this

Zero-spacing and endpoint-gap controls exclude collision and boundary strata. They do not prevent analytic cancellation among separated points.

A simple finite-dimensional model shows the issue. Let normalized gaps satisfy pairwise separation, and define

\[
G(d_1,d_2,d_3)=d_1+d_2-2d_3.
\]

Take

\[
d_1=0,\qquad d_2=2,\qquad d_3=1+\varepsilon.
\]

The points remain separated for small \(\varepsilon\), but

\[
G=-2\varepsilon
\]

can be arbitrarily small. Thus spacing excludes

\[
d_i=d_j,
\]

but it does not exclude small values of analytic coefficient functions.

The finite-core functions \(F_N\) are exactly of this type: analytic cancellation functions of normalized source/core parameters, not just denominators or pairwise gaps.

---

# 3. Discreteness of zeta zeros is also insufficient

A discrete sampled set can approach an analytic zero locus arbitrarily fast. For example,

\[
\theta_n=(e^{-n},1/2)
\]

is discrete in a compact set and never lies on

\[
\mathcal Z=\{x=0\},
\]

but

\[
\operatorname{dist}(\theta_n,\mathcal Z)=e^{-n}.
\]

So “zeta zeros are discrete” does not imply

\[
|F_N(\theta(m),Q)|\ge \Lambda(m,Q).
\]

The missing input is a Diophantine-type small-value exclusion for the actual normalized zero configurations.

---

# 4. Remez / Łojasiewicz / volume estimates are not enough

Łojasiewicz gives lower bounds in terms of distance to the zero locus:

\[
\|F(\theta,Q)\|
\gtrsim
\operatorname{dist}(\theta,\{F=0\})^\mu.
\]

Remez-type inequalities can give volume estimates for small-value sets:

\[
\operatorname{vol}\{\theta:\|F(\theta,Q)\|<\epsilon\}
\ll \epsilon^\alpha.
\]

But the proof needs pointwise exclusion for actual samples:

\[
\theta(m)\notin \{\|F\|<\Lambda(m,Q)\}.
\]

A density theorem would only help if it were strong enough to imply

\[
\#\{m\le T:\theta(m)\in\{\|F\|<\Lambda(m,Q)\}\}<1
\]

for the relevant range. That would require effective equidistribution/non-concentration of actual zeta core parameters at the very small scale \(\Lambda(m,Q)\). No such theorem is present.

So a weaker density result is not enough for the current global RH-exclusion strategy, because a single bad finite core could remain as a counterexample branch.

---

# 5. The exact missing theorem

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Sampled finite-core coefficient non-concentration]
\label{thm:sampled-finite-core-coefficient-nonconcentration}
Let \(\Theta_k\) be a compact nonsingular normalized actual-source
\(k\)-core stratum.  For
\[
1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1
\]
define
\[
F_N(\theta,Q)
=
c_{\core,2N-1}(\theta)
+
\sum_{j\ge1}
c_{\core,2N-1+2j}(\theta)
h_j(1^2,\dots,N^2)Q^{-2j}.
\]
Then every actual zeta finite-core parameter \(\theta(m)\in\Theta_k\)
satisfies one of:
\[
\theta(m)\in\mathcal Z_k,
\]
\[
\theta(m)\in\mathcal E_{\rm geom},
\]
or
\[
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
|F_N(\theta(m),Q)|
\ge
C_*
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right).
\]
\end{theorem}
```

This is not a formal analytic consequence of the current framework. It is a new arithmetic/sampling separation theorem.

---

# 6. The unresolved coefficient-small branch

```latex
\begin{definition}[Coefficient-small finite-core branch]
\label{def:coefficient-small-finite-core-branch}
Let \(\Theta_k\) be a compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum.
Define \(\mathcal N_k^{\coef}(m,Q)\) to be the set of actual zeta finite-core
parameters \(\theta(m)\in\Theta_k\) such that
\[
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom},
\]
but
\[
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
|F_N(\theta(m),Q)|
<
C_*
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right).
\]
\end{definition}
```

This is the precise branch Finite-Core A cannot eliminate with existing tools.

---

## Bottom line

Finite-Core A does **not** close the finite-core blocker.

The proof requires a new pointwise theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{actual zeta finite-core samples avoid analytic coefficient-small sets at scale }\Lambda(m,Q).
}
\]

Zero-spacing, endpoint gaps, compactness, discreteness, and volume estimates do not supply this. Density estimates would only suffice if strong enough to make the number of bad sampled cores strictly less than one, which is not available in the current draft.

## Finite-Core A — sampled coefficient non-concentration attack

\right\}.

The attached consolidation explicitly identifies this as the finite-core target and separates it from finite determinacy and projective detection, both of which are already done. 

---

# 1. Exact theorem under attack

For

\[
F_N(\theta,Q)
=
c_{\core,2N-1}(\theta)
+
\sum_{j\ge1}
c_{\core,2N-1+2j}(\theta)
h_j(1^2,\dots,N^2)Q^{-2j},
\]

define

\[
\Lambda(m,Q)
=
C_*
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right).
\]

The theorem needed is:

\[
\boxed{
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
|F_N(\theta(m),Q)|
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
}
\]

This is a **pointwise sampled small-value exclusion theorem** for the actual zeta core map

\[
m\mapsto \theta(m).
\]

It is stronger than finite determinacy, stronger than pairwise zero-spacing, and stronger than compactness.

---

# 2. Zero-spacing and endpoint gaps do not imply coefficient non-concentration

Zero-spacing and endpoint-gap controls exclude collision and boundary strata, i.e. they help keep

\[
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

But the functions \(F_N\) define analytic cancellation loci, not merely collision loci.

A toy model shows the gap. Let

\[
G(d_1,d_2,d_3)=d_1+d_2-2d_3.
\]

Take

\[
d_1=0,\qquad d_2=2,\qquad d_3=1+\varepsilon.
\]

The points remain separated as \(\varepsilon\to0\), but

\[
G=-2\varepsilon
\]

can be arbitrarily small. Thus pairwise spacing does not prevent analytic cancellation. The finite-core functions \(F_N\) are of this cancellation type.

So the implication

\[
\text{zero-spacing + endpoint regularity}
\Longrightarrow
\max_N |F_N|\ge\Lambda
\]

is false as a formal principle.

---

# 3. Discreteness of zeta zeros is too weak

The zeta zeros are discrete, but discreteness does not imply lower bounds against analytic subvarieties.

A discrete sequence can approach a zero set arbitrarily fast:

\[
\theta_n=(e^{-n},1/2),
\qquad
\mathcal Z=\{x=0\}.
\]

Then

\[
\theta_n\notin\mathcal Z,
\qquad
\operatorname{dist}(\theta_n,\mathcal Z)=e^{-n}.
\]

So “actual samples are discrete” does not yield

\[
\max_N |F_N(\theta(m),Q)|\ge\Lambda(m,Q).
\]

The missing theorem is Diophantine/sampling in nature: actual normalized zero configurations must avoid certain analytic small-value tubes at a specified scale.

---

# 4. Remez / Łojasiewicz / volume estimates do not give pointwise exclusion

For analytic \(F=(F_1,\dots,F_M)\), Łojasiewicz gives

\[
\|F(\theta,Q)\|
\gtrsim
\operatorname{dist}(\theta,\{F=0\})^\mu.
\]

Remez-type estimates may give a volume bound:

\[
\operatorname{vol}\{\theta:\|F(\theta,Q)\|<\varepsilon\}
\ll \varepsilon^\alpha.
\]

But the proof needs:

\[
\theta(m)\notin\{\|F\|<\Lambda(m,Q)\}
\]

for every actual off-line finite-core sample.

A volume or density bound would only suffice if paired with an effective equidistribution theorem strong enough to show

\[
\#\{m\le T:\theta(m)\in\{\|F\|<\Lambda(m,Q)\}\}<1.
\]

No such equidistribution or arithmetic non-concentration theorem appears in the current proof architecture. Therefore measure-small is not enough; the proof needs pointwise exclusion.

---

# 5. Interaction-fed cancellation is a live mechanism

The finite-determinacy coefficient vector can be decomposed schematically as

\[
C_{\rm fd}(\theta)
=
P_{\rm fd}(\theta)+J_{\rm fd}(\theta),
\]

where \(P_{\rm fd}\) is the pair-like / one-body part and \(J_{\rm fd}\) contains interaction terms. At first order,

\[
c_{\core,1}
=
\sum_\nu a_\nu K(d_\nu)+J_1,
\qquad
J_1=[s]\Phi_K(\mathcal I_{\ge2}).
\]

The current consolidated state says \(J_1\) is not proved zero, sign-controlled, or incidence-controlled. 

Hence the small-value branch can be fed by

\[
J_{\rm fd}(\theta)\approx -P_{\rm fd}(\theta)
\]

without forcing collision, endpoint failure, patch boundary, or other controlled incidence.

This does not prove actual zeta realizes the branch. It shows that current source geometry does not exclude it.

---

The missing theorem should be stated directly as sampled non-concentration:

```latex
\left(

{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right).
\]
\end{theorem}
```

This is not a consequence of existing finite determinacy or compactness. It is the missing arithmetic/sampling input.

The current consolidated state says the finite-core proof needs exactly this pointwise lower bound, or equivalently radial anti-smallness. 

---

# 2. Zero-spacing and endpoint gaps are insufficient

Zero-spacing and endpoint-gap controls exclude collision or boundary degeneration. They do not exclude analytic cancellation.

A simple model:

\[
G(d_1,d_2,d_3)=d_1+d_2-2d_3.
\]

Take

\[
d_1=0,\qquad d_2=2,\qquad d_3=1+\varepsilon.
\]

The three points remain separated as \(\varepsilon\to0\), but

\[
G(d_1,d_2,d_3)=-2\varepsilon
\]

can be arbitrarily small.

Thus pairwise spacing can prove

\[
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal E_{\rm collision},
\]

but it cannot prove

\[
\max_N |F_N(\theta(m),Q)|\ge \Lambda(m,Q).
\]

The functions \(F_N\) are analytic cancellation functions of the finite-core parameters, not merely gap denominators.

---

# 3. Discreteness of zeros is also insufficient

Discreteness gives no effective lower bound against analytic subvarieties.

A discrete sequence may approach a zero set faster than any prescribed scale:

\[
\theta_n=(e^{-n},1/2),
\qquad
\mathcal Z=\{x=0\}.
\]

Then

\[
\theta_n\notin\mathcal Z,
\]

but

\[
\operatorname{dist}(\theta_n,\mathcal Z)=e^{-n}.
\]

So even if actual zeta finite-core parameters are sampled discretely, discreteness alone gives no inequality of the form

\[
|F_N(\theta(m),Q)|\ge \Lambda(m,Q).
\]

The missing input is Diophantine/sampling non-concentration, not ordinary discreteness.

---

# 4. Remez / Łojasiewicz / volume estimates are not enough

Łojasiewicz gives a geometric relation:

\[
\|F(\theta,Q)\|
\gtrsim
\operatorname{dist}(\theta,\{F=0\})^\mu.
\]

Remez-type estimates can give a measure bound:

\[
\operatorname{vol}
\{\theta:\|F(\theta,Q)\|<\epsilon\}
\ll
\epsilon^\alpha.
\]

Neither is pointwise.

To use a volume theorem, the proof would additionally need an effective distribution estimate for actual samples:

\[
\#\{m\le T:\theta(m)\in U\}
\le
C\,\operatorname{vol}(U)\,\#\{m\le T\}
+
\mathrm{error}(T,U).
\]

Even that would only close the RH branch if the bound were strong enough to give

\[
\#\{m\le T:\max_N |F_N(\theta(m),Q)|<\Lambda(m,Q)\}<1
\]

in the relevant range. No such equidistribution/non-concentration theorem appears in the current proof state.

So a density theorem is **not enough** unless it is strong enough to eliminate all bad samples, not merely make them sparse.

---

# 5. Interaction-fed cancellation remains a live mechanism

The finite coefficient vector may be decomposed schematically as

\[
C_{\rm fd}(\theta)
=
P_{\rm fd}(\theta)+J_{\rm fd}(\theta).
\]

At first order,

\[
c_{\core,1}
=
\sum_\nu a_\nu K(d_\nu)+J_1,
\qquad
J_1=[s]\Phi_K(\mathcal I_{\ge2}).
\]

The current state says interaction terms can formally cancel the pair-like vector,

\[
J_{\rm fd}\approx -P_{\rm fd},
\]

without forcing controlled incidence. 

This means the branch

\[
0<
\max_N |F_N(\theta(m),Q)|
<
\Lambda(m,Q)
\]

is not merely a pathological analytic possibility; it is compatible with the known unresolved interaction mechanism.

## Finite-Core A — continued attack

### New reduction

The sampled coefficient non-concentration theorem is equivalent, up to constants, to **radial finite-determinacy norm anti-smallness** once \(Q\) is large enough. This collapses the sampling problem to a single scalar size problem:

\[
\boxed{
\|H_{\core,\theta(m)}\|_{\rm fd}
\not\ll
\Lambda(m,Q)
}
\]

outside

\[
\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

So the finite-core branch is no longer about finding the right \(N\); projective detection chooses \(N\). It is about proving the actual sampled finite-core germ is not too small. The attached instructions explicitly identify sampled coefficient non-concentration / radial anti-smallness as the active finite-core blocker. 

---

# 1. Equivalence of coefficient non-concentration and radial anti-smallness

Recall

\[
F_N(\theta,Q)
=
c_{\core,2N-1}(\theta)
+
\sum_{j\ge1}
c_{\core,2N-1+2j}(\theta)
h_j(1^2,\dots,N^2)Q^{-2j}.
\]

Define

\[
\|H_{\core,\theta}\|_{\rm fd}
=
\max_{0\le r\le R_{\Theta_k}}
|c_{\core,2r+1}(\theta)|.
\]

For bounded

\[
1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1,
\]

tail control gives

\[
|F_N(\theta,Q)-c_{\core,2N-1}(\theta)|
\le
K_{\Theta_k}Q^{-2}\|H_{\core,\theta}\|_{\rm fd}.
\]

For \(Q\ge Q_0(\Theta_k)\), choose \(N_*\) such that

\[
|c_{\core,2N_*-1}(\theta)|
=
\|H_{\core,\theta}\|_{\rm fd}.
\]

Then

\[
|F_{N_*}(\theta,Q)|
\ge
\frac12
\|H_{\core,\theta}\|_{\rm fd}.
\]

Conversely,

\[
\max_N |F_N(\theta,Q)|
\le
(1+K_{\Theta_k}Q^{-2})
\|H_{\core,\theta}\|_{\rm fd}.
\]

Therefore, for large \(Q\),

\[
\boxed{
\max_N |F_N(\theta,Q)|
\asymp_{\Theta_k}
\|H_{\core,\theta}\|_{\rm fd}.
}
\]

So sampled coefficient non-concentration is equivalent to

\[
\boxed{
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\|H_{\core,\theta(m)}\|_{\rm fd}\gtrsim \Lambda(m,Q).
}
\]

where

\[
\Lambda(m,Q)
=
C_*
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right).
\]

This is a useful simplification: the finite-core problem is a **radial non-smallness theorem**, not a projector-selection problem.

---

# 2. Contradiction extraction

Assume the theorem fails. Then there is a sequence of actual zeta finite-core parameters

\[
\theta_n=\theta(m_n)
\]

such that

\[
\theta_n\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom},
\]

but

\[
0<
\|H_{\core,\theta_n}\|_{\rm fd}
<
\Lambda(m_n,Q_n).
\]

If

\[
\Lambda(m_n,Q_n)\to0,
\]

then

\[
\|H_{\core,\theta_n}\|_{\rm fd}\to0.
\]

By compactness of \(\Theta_k\), after passing to a subsequence,

\[
\theta_n\to\theta_\infty\in\Theta_k.
\]

Since

\[
\|H_{\core,\theta_n}\|_{\rm fd}\to0,
\]

finite determinacy implies

\[
\theta_\infty\in\mathcal Z_k.
\]

Thus every infinite failure sequence accumulates on

\[
\mathcal Z_k\cap\overline{\Theta_k\setminus\mathcal E_{\rm geom}}.
\]

This extraction is valid, but it does not close the branch. To close it, the draft would need one of:

\[
\mathcal Z_k\subset \mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\]

plus a calibrated collar exclusion around \(\mathcal E_{\rm geom}\), or a direct sampled lower bound for

\[
\|H_{\core,\theta(m)}\|_{\rm fd}.
\]

Neither is presently available.

---

# 3. Why exact zero control would still be insufficient

Suppose optimistically that one proved

\[
\mathcal Z_k\subset\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

This would show the failure sequence accumulates at controlled incidence. But it would not prove

\[
\theta_n\in\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

A sequence can remain outside a closed incidence set while approaching it at a rate smaller than \(\Lambda(m,Q)\).

Formal model:

\[
\Theta=[0,1]^2,
\qquad
\mathcal Z=\mathcal E_{\rm geom}=\{x=0\},
\]

\[
\theta_n=(\varepsilon_n,1/2),
\qquad
0<\varepsilon_n<\Lambda_n.
\]

Then

\[
\theta_n\notin\mathcal Z\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom},
\]

but

\[
\|H_{\theta_n}\|_{\rm fd}\asymp \varepsilon_n<\Lambda_n.
\]

So even exact zero-anomaly control is not enough. The proof needs **collar exclusion**:

\[
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\operatorname{dist}(\theta(m),\mathcal E_{\rm geom})
\gtrsim \Lambda(m,Q)^{1/\mu}.
\]

No such theorem is in the draft.

---

# 4. Density / volume estimates still do not close the pointwise branch

Let

\[
B_\Lambda
=
\{\theta\in\Theta_k:\|H_{\core,\theta}\|_{\rm fd}<\Lambda\}.
\]

Remez or Łojasiewicz methods may give

\[
\operatorname{vol}(B_\Lambda)
\ll
\Lambda^\alpha.
\]

To use this for actual samples, one would need an effective distribution theorem:

\[
\#\{m\le T:\theta(m)\in B_\Lambda\}
\le
C\Lambda^\alpha\,\#\{m\le T\}
+
\mathrm{Err}(T,\Lambda).
\]

But the RH proof needs pointwise exclusion of any bad finite-core configuration. A density bound would suffice only if it implied

\[
C\Lambda^\alpha\,\#\{m\le T\}
+
\mathrm{Err}(T,\Lambda)
<1.
\]

No such distribution theorem appears in the current proof-state. Therefore density non-concentration is not enough unless it is strong enough to become pointwise at the calibrated scale.

---

# 5. The missing theorem can be stated more cleanly

Since

\[
\max_N|F_N|\asymp \|H_{\core,\theta}\|_{\rm fd},
\]

the theorem should be stated radially:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Pointwise radial finite-core anti-smallness]
\label{thm:pointwise-radial-finite-core-anti-smallness}
Let \(\Theta_k\) be a compact nonsingular normalized actual-source
\(k\)-core stratum.  For every actual zeta finite-core parameter
\[
\theta(m)\in\Theta_k,
\]
one of the following holds:
\[
\theta(m)\in\mathcal Z_k,
\]
\[
\theta(m)\in\mathcal E_{\rm geom},
\]
or
\[
\|H_{\core,\theta(m)}\|_{\rm fd}
\ge
C_{\Theta_k}
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right).
\]
\end{theorem}
```

Equivalent coefficient form:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Pointwise sampled finite-core coefficient non-concentration]
\label{thm:pointwise-sampled-finite-core-coefficient-nonconcentration}
For every actual zeta finite-core parameter
\[
\theta(m)\in\Theta_k,
\]
one has
\[
\theta(m)\in\mathcal Z_k
\quad\text{or}\quad
\theta(m)\in\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\]
or
\[
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
|F_N(\theta(m),Q)|
\ge
C_*
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right).
\]
\end{theorem}
```

The radial theorem and coefficient theorem are equivalent up to the already-handled \(Q^{-2}\) tail control.

---

# 6. Precise unresolved branch

```latex
\begin{definition}[Radially small finite-core branch]
\label{def:radially-small-finite-core-branch}
Let \(\Theta_k\) be a compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum.
Define
\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm rad}(m,Q)
=
\left\{
\theta(m)\in\Theta_k:
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom},
\quad
0<\|H_{\core,\theta(m)}\|_{\rm fd}<\Lambda(m,Q)
\right\},
\]
where
\[
\Lambda(m,Q)
=
C_*
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right).
\]
\end{definition}
```

And, equivalently,

```latex
\begin{definition}[Coefficient-small finite-core branch]
\label{def:coefficient-small-finite-core-branch}
Define
\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm coef}(m,Q)
=
\left\{
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}:
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}|F_N(\theta(m),Q)|<\Lambda(m,Q)
\right\}.
\]
\end{definition}
```

For \(Q\ge Q_0(\Theta_k)\),

\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm rad}
\quad\text{and}\quad
\mathcal N_k^{\rm coef}
\]

are the same branch up to constants.

---

# 7. What would actually prove it?

One of the following new inputs is necessary:

### A. Pointwise arithmetic separation

For every analytic coefficient vector arising from finite-core correction,

\[
\|H_{\core,\theta(m)}\|_{\rm fd}
\ge \Lambda(m,Q)
\]

outside controlled incidence.

### B. Source-level anti-cancellation

A theorem showing

\[
P_{\rm fd}(\theta)+J_{\rm fd}(\theta)
\]

cannot be small unless controlled incidence occurs.

This would directly attack the interaction-fed mechanism.

### C. Effective equidistribution strong enough to imply zero bad samples

A distribution theorem for

\[
m\mapsto\theta(m)
\]

with error strong enough that the small-value tube contains no actual samples at the calibrated scale.

A weak density theorem is insufficient.

---

## Bottom line

The continued attack reduces the finite-core branch to the following exact statement:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal N_k^{\rm rad}(m,Q)=\varnothing
}
\]

or equivalently

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal N_k^{\rm coef}(m,Q)=\varnothing.
}
\]

The draft currently supplies no pointwise arithmetic/sampling theorem, no collar exclusion, and no interaction anti-cancellation theorem strong enough to prove this.

## Assistant (2026-04-25 12:50:31)

I’ll now attack independence from the current axioms: build a formal finite-core model satisfying the stated controls but violating radial anti-smallness. If such a model fits the paper’s present obligations, the missing theorem is genuinely external rather than a bookkeeping gap.

_Thought for 10s_

## Finite-Core A — continued attack via formal independence model

### Result

The sampled coefficient non-concentration theorem is **not derivable from the current finite-core axioms**. More strongly, one can build a formal finite-core model satisfying the current listed controls — compact same-scale stratum, finite determinacy, non-collision, endpoint-gap regularity, nonzero \(M,W,K_v,T_v\), nonsingular whitening, and \(\theta\notin\mathcal Z_k\) — while violating the required lower bound

\[
\max_N |F_N(\theta(m),Q)|\ge \Lambda(m,Q).
\]

This shows the missing theorem is not a table/normalization issue. It is a genuine **pointwise arithmetic/sampling separation** or **source-level anti-cancellation** input. The attached finite-core prompt identifies exactly this target and says not to re-prove finite determinacy or projective detection. 

---

# 1. Abstract finite-core data

Let

\[
C_{\rm fd}(\theta)
=
(c_{\core,1},c_{\core,3},\ldots,c_{\core,2R+1})(\theta)
\in \mathbb C^{R+1}.
\]

Decompose

\[
C_{\rm fd}(\theta)
=
P_{\rm fd}(\theta)+J_{\rm fd}(\theta),
\]

where \(P_{\rm fd}\) is the pair-like / one-body vector and \(J_{\rm fd}\) is the interaction vector. At first order this matches

\[
c_{\core,1}
=
\sum_\nu a_\nu K(d_\nu)+J_1,
\qquad
J_1=[s]\Phi_K(\mathcal I_{\ge2}).
\]

The current proof-state does not prove \(J_{\rm fd}=0\), sign control, cone control, or incidence containment. The latest consolidation explicitly says the finite-core mechanism can be

\[
J_{\rm fd}\approx -P_{\rm fd}
\]

without forcing controlled incidence. 

---

# 2. Formal countermodel to derivability

Fix a compact nonsingular patch \(\Theta_k\) with all controlled incidence functions bounded away from zero:

\[
M,W,K_v,T_v\neq0,
\]

and no collision, no endpoint-gap collapse, no patch boundary, no amplitude drop, no whitening singularity,

\[
c\neq0,
\qquad
A_5^{\mathfrak f}\neq0,
\]

and no hidden-rank jump.

Let \(P_{\rm fd}(\theta)\equiv P_0\neq0\) be a fixed pair-like vector. Introduce one free interaction parameter \(\varepsilon\) and define

\[
J_{\rm fd}(\varepsilon)
=
-P_0+\varepsilon e_1,
\]

where \(e_1=(1,0,\ldots,0)\). Then

\[
C_{\rm fd}(\varepsilon)
=
P_0+J_{\rm fd}(\varepsilon)
=
\varepsilon e_1.
\]

Thus

\[
\|H_{\core,\theta(\varepsilon)}\|_{\rm fd}
=
\|C_{\rm fd}(\varepsilon)\|_\infty
=
|\varepsilon|.
\]

For every \(\varepsilon\neq0\),

\[
\theta(\varepsilon)\notin\mathcal Z_k,
\]

because the finite-determinacy vector is nonzero. Also, by construction,

\[
\theta(\varepsilon)\notin\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

But choosing

\[
0<|\varepsilon|<\Lambda(m,Q)
\]

gives

\[
0<
\|H_{\core,\theta(\varepsilon)}\|_{\rm fd}
<
\Lambda(m,Q),
\]

so

\[
\theta(\varepsilon)\in\mathcal N_k^{\rm rad}(m,Q).
\]

For \(Q\) large, projective detection gives

\[
\max_N |F_N(\theta(\varepsilon),Q)|
\asymp |\varepsilon|,
\]

so the coefficient-small branch also occurs:

\[
\max_N |F_N(\theta(\varepsilon),Q)|
<
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]

This is a formal model of

\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm coef}(m,Q)\neq\varnothing.
\]

---

# 3. Why this model is compatible with the current obligations

The model does **not** violate finite determinacy:

\[
C_{\rm fd}(\varepsilon)=0
\Longleftrightarrow
\varepsilon=0
\Longleftrightarrow
H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0.
\]

It does **not** violate projective detection:

\[
C_{\rm fd}(\varepsilon)\neq0
\]

is detected by the first coefficient direction.

It does **not** violate zero-spacing or endpoint gaps, because those are held fixed away from degeneration.

It does **not** violate controlled incidence exclusions, because

\[
M,W,K_v,T_v,c,A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

are all fixed nonzero, and the construction stays away from collision, endpoint, patch, whitening, and rank-jump strata.

The only thing it violates is the desired **radial lower bound**

\[
\|H_{\core,\theta(m)}\|_{\rm fd}
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]

So radial anti-smallness is independent of the current listed controls.

---

# 4. What would rule out this model?

One needs a theorem forbidding interaction cancellation of the whole finite-determinacy vector:

\[
P_{\rm fd}(\theta)+J_{\rm fd}(\theta)
\]

from becoming small unless controlled incidence occurs.

A theorem-ready version is:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Finite-core interaction anti-cancellation]
\label{thm:finite-core-interaction-anti-cancellation}
Let \(\Theta_k\) be a compact nonsingular normalized actual-source
\(k\)-core stratum.  Write
\[
C_{\rm fd}(\theta)=P_{\rm fd}(\theta)+J_{\rm fd}(\theta),
\]
where
\[
C_{\rm fd}(\theta)
=
(c_{\core,1},c_{\core,3},\ldots,c_{\core,2R_{\Theta_k}+1})(\theta).
\]
For every actual zeta finite-core parameter
\[
\theta(m)\in\Theta_k\setminus(\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}),
\]
one has
\[
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
C_{\Theta_k}\Lambda(m,Q).
\]
\end{theorem}
```

Equivalently, one needs the sampled coefficient theorem:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Pointwise sampled finite-core coefficient non-concentration]
\label{thm:pointwise-sampled-finite-core-coefficient-nonconcentration}
For every actual zeta finite-core parameter
\[
\theta(m)\in\Theta_k\setminus(\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}),
\]
\[
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
|F_N(\theta(m),Q)|
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]
\end{theorem}
```

These are not consequences of the present paper-state.

---

# 5. Exact unresolved branch

```latex
\begin{definition}[Interaction-fed radially small finite-core branch]
\label{def:interaction-fed-radially-small-finite-core-branch}
Let
\[
C_{\rm fd}(\theta)=P_{\rm fd}(\theta)+J_{\rm fd}(\theta)
\]
be the finite-determinacy coefficient vector.  Define
\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm int\text{-}rad}(m,Q)
\]
to be the set of actual zeta finite-core parameters
\[
\theta(m)\in\Theta_k\setminus(\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom})
\]
such that
\[
0<
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
<
\Lambda(m,Q),
\]
where
\[
\Lambda(m,Q)
=
C_*
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right).
\]
\end{definition}
```

This is a sub-branch of

\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm rad}(m,Q)
\]

and a mechanism for

\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm coef}(m,Q).
\]

---

# 6. Relation to \(J_1\)

Controlling only

\[
J_1=[s]\Phi_K(\mathcal I_{\ge2})
\]

is not enough unless the theorem extends to the full vector

\[
J_{\rm fd}
=
(J_1,J_3,\ldots,J_{2R+1}).
\]

A first-order interaction theorem could prevent

\[
c_{\core,1}
\]

from cancelling, but the finite-determinacy norm can still be small through higher-order cancellations if

\[
J_3,J_5,\ldots,J_{2R+1}
\]

remain uncontrolled.

Thus the missing finite-core theorem must control the **whole finite vector**, not just \(J_1\).

---

## Bottom line

Finite-Core A has a formal independence model:

\[
C_{\rm fd}=P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}
=
\varepsilon e_1
\]

with all controlled incidences avoided.

Therefore the sampled coefficient non-concentration theorem is not derivable from the current axioms. The proof needs a new pointwise input:

\[
\boxed{
\text{finite-core interaction anti-cancellation / sampled coefficient non-concentration.}
}
\]

Without it, the live branch is

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal N_k^{\rm int\text{-}rad}(m,Q)
\subset
\mathcal N_k^{\rm rad}(m,Q)
\sim
\mathcal N_k^{\rm coef}(m,Q).
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-25 12:51:41)

I’ll now test whether the formal independence model can be blocked by the fact that actual zeta cores may have fewer degrees of freedom than an arbitrary \(J_{\rm fd}\). The key question is whether the interaction vector is locally free enough to cancel the pair-like vector, or constrained by the source map.

_Thought for 9s_

## Finite-Core A — continued attack on interaction freedom

### New target

The previous formal model used an arbitrary interaction vector

\[
J_{\rm fd}\approx -P_{\rm fd}.
\]

The natural objection is that actual zeta finite-core interaction data may not be free enough to realize such cancellation. So the sharper question is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the actual source map constrain }J_{\rm fd}
\text{ so strongly that }P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}
\text{ cannot be small outside }\mathcal E_{\rm geom}?
}
\]

I do **not** find such a constraint in the current proof-state. The latest instructions explicitly identify the finite-core blocker as sampled coefficient non-concentration / radial anti-smallness and note that interaction terms can formally cancel the finite vector without controlled incidence. 

---

# 1. Reformulate as a source-map rank problem

Let the actual finite-core parameter be

\[
\theta\in\Theta_k.
\]

Write

\[
C_{\rm fd}(\theta)
=
P_{\rm fd}(\theta)+J_{\rm fd}(\theta)
\in \mathbb C^{R_{\Theta_k}+1},
\]

where

\[
C_{\rm fd}(\theta)
=
(c_{\core,1},c_{\core,3},\ldots,c_{\core,2R_{\Theta_k}+1})(\theta).
\]

The desired non-concentration theorem is equivalent to a pointwise lower bound

\[
\|C_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q)
\]

outside

\[
\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

Define the interaction source map

\[
\mathcal J:\Theta_k\to\mathbb C^{R_{\Theta_k}+1},
\qquad
\mathcal J(\theta)=J_{\rm fd}(\theta).
\]

Then radial smallness occurs when

\[
\mathcal J(\theta)
\approx
-P_{\rm fd}(\theta).
\]

So to rule it out structurally, the paper would need one of:

\[
-P_{\rm fd}(\theta)
\notin
\overline{\mathcal J(\Theta_k)}
\quad
\text{outside }\mathcal E_{\rm geom},
\]

or a quantitative version:

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\bigl(
-P_{\rm fd}(\theta),
\mathcal J(\Theta_k)
\bigr)
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]

No such separation theorem is currently present.

---

# 2. Local differential test

Suppose there is a candidate cancellation point

\[
\theta_0\notin\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\]

with

\[
C_{\rm fd}(\theta_0)=0.
\]

Then

\[
\theta_0\in\mathcal Z_k.
\]

The local question is whether \(\mathcal Z_k\) is forced into controlled incidence. Linearizing,

\[
dC_{\rm fd}(\theta_0)
=
dP_{\rm fd}(\theta_0)+dJ_{\rm fd}(\theta_0).
\]

If

\[
dC_{\rm fd}(\theta_0)
\]

has nontrivial kernel transverse to \(\mathcal E_{\rm geom}\), then there are analytic arcs

\[
\theta(t)\notin\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\]

with

\[
C_{\rm fd}(\theta(t))=O(t^2).
\]

Even if the zero itself is controlled, near-zero branches can persist unless the transverse derivative is bounded below at the sampled scale.

Thus the needed condition is not merely

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{-1}(0)\subset\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

It is a quantitative transversality condition:

\[
\|dC_{\rm fd}(\theta)v\|
\ge c\|v\|
\]

in directions away from controlled incidence, or a higher-order analogue on singular strata.

The current draft has no such finite-vector transversality theorem.

---

# 3. Rank deficiency is enough to create near-smallness

If

\[
\operatorname{rank} dC_{\rm fd}(\theta_0)
<
R_{\Theta_k}+1
\]

at a zero-anomaly point \(\theta_0\), then the zero set or near-zero set may have positive-dimensional branches. Unless those branches are contained in \(\mathcal E_{\rm geom}\), actual samples can pass arbitrarily close.

Even if \(dC_{\rm fd}\) has full rank, one still needs sampled separation from the zero set. Full rank gives a local estimate

\[
\|C_{\rm fd}(\theta)\|
\asymp
\operatorname{dist}(\theta,\mathcal Z_k),
\]

but it does not prove

\[
\operatorname{dist}(\theta(m),\mathcal Z_k)
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{rank/transversality helps convert distance to coefficient size,}
}
\]

but

\[
\boxed{
\text{it does not produce pointwise sampled separation.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Interaction freedom at first order already defeats cone-only control

At first order,

\[
c_{\core,1}
=
\sum_\nu a_\nu K(d_\nu)+J_1.
\]

Even if

\[
\sum_\nu a_\nu K(d_\nu)
\]

lies in a favorable half-plane, the interaction scalar \(J_1\) is not currently shown to lie in the same half-plane or in a controlled subcone.

Thus a local source model with one interaction parameter

\[
J_1=-\sum_\nu a_\nu K(d_\nu)+\varepsilon
\]

is not excluded by the present finite-core axioms.

The same issue extends to the full vector:

\[
J_{\rm fd}
=
-P_{\rm fd}
+
\varepsilon v,
\]

with

\[
0<\varepsilon<\Lambda(m,Q).
\]

Unless the source construction proves that \(J_{\rm fd}\) is constrained to a cone separated from \(-P_{\rm fd}\), radial smallness remains possible.

---

# 5. What theorem would block interaction freedom?

The precise missing theorem is a finite-vector anti-cancellation theorem.

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Finite-vector interaction anti-cancellation]
Let \(\Theta_k\) be a compact nonsingular normalized actual-source \(k\)-core
stratum.  Write
\[
C_{\rm fd}(\theta)=P_{\rm fd}(\theta)+J_{\rm fd}(\theta).
\]
Then for every actual zeta finite-core parameter
\[
\theta(m)\in\Theta_k\setminus(\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}),
\]
one has
\[
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]
\end{theorem}
```

This is equivalent to the sampled coefficient non-concentration theorem, but it states the obstruction mechanism explicitly.

A more structural sufficient theorem would be:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Interaction cone separation]
On each compact nonsingular \(k\)-core stratum, there is a closed cone
\(\mathcal C_{\rm int}\subset\mathbb C^{R_{\Theta_k}+1}\) such that
\[
J_{\rm fd}(\theta)\in\mathcal C_{\rm int},
\]
and
\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
-P_{\rm fd}(\theta),
\mathcal C_{\rm int}
\right)
\ge c_{\Theta_k}>0
\]
outside \(\mathcal E_{\rm geom}\).  Then radial sampled anti-smallness holds
after scaling by the calibrated factor.
\end{theorem}
```

The draft does not establish such a cone or separation.

---

# 6. A sharper bad branch

The unresolved branch should explicitly remember that cancellation is vectorial:

\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm vec}(m,Q)
=
\left\{
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}:
0<
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
<
\Lambda(m,Q)
\right\}.
\]

This is more informative than the generic coefficient-small branch because it identifies the cancellation mechanism.

```latex
\begin{definition}[Vector-cancellation finite-core branch]
Let
\[
C_{\rm fd}=P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}
\]
be the finite-determinacy coefficient vector.  Define
\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm vec}(m,Q)
\]
to be the set of actual zeta finite-core parameters
\[
\theta(m)\in\Theta_k\setminus(\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom})
\]
such that
\[
0<
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
<
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]
\end{definition}
```

This branch is not eliminated by finite determinacy, compactness, zero-spacing, endpoint-gap controls, or \(N\)-point positivity.

---

# 7. What FC-A can now honestly conclude

The attack reduces the finite-core problem to one of three possible missing inputs:

### Option 1 — arithmetic sampled separation

\[
\theta(m)
\]

does not approach the analytic small-value set of \(C_{\rm fd}\) at scale \(\Lambda(m,Q)\).

### Option 2 — source-level cone/separation

\[
J_{\rm fd}
\]

lies in a cone or submanifold separated from

\[
-P_{\rm fd}
\]

outside controlled incidence.

### Option 3 — incidence containment

Every point or arc satisfying

\[
P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}=0
\]

or

\[
P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}\approx0
\]

belongs to, or approaches at calibrated scale, \(\mathcal E_{\rm geom}\).

The current draft proves none of these.

---

## Bottom line

The finite-core radial/sample blocker can now be stated as a **finite-vector interaction cancellation problem**:

\[
\boxed{
P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))
\approx 0
}
\]

outside controlled incidence.

Unless the paper proves a cone, rank, incidence, or arithmetic sampling theorem preventing this cancellation at scale \(\Lambda(m,Q)\), the branch

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal N_k^{\rm vec}(m,Q)
}
\]

remains live.

## Finite-Core A — continued attack via ideal containment

### New reduction

The finite-core obstruction can be split into an **exact algebraic problem** and a **calibrated analytic/sampling problem**.

The exact algebraic problem is:

\[
C_{\rm fd}(\theta)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\theta\in\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

The calibrated analytic/sampling problem is stronger:

\[
0<\|C_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty<\Lambda(m,Q)
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\theta(m)\in\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\]

or at least

\[
\theta(m)
\text{ lies inside a controlled calibrated collar of }
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

The present draft-state gives neither. The latest deployment identifies sampled coefficient non-concentration / radial anti-smallness as the finite-core blocker, and the prior consolidation states that interaction terms can feed this branch by \(J_{\rm fd}\approx -P_{\rm fd}\). 

---

# 1. Algebraic exact-zero formulation

Let

\[
C_{\rm fd}
=
(c_{\core,1},c_{\core,3},\ldots,c_{\core,2R_{\Theta_k}+1})
=
P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}.
\]

Let \(I_C\) be the ideal generated by the finite-core coefficients:

\[
I_C
=
\langle
c_{\core,1},
c_{\core,3},
\ldots,
c_{\core,2R_{\Theta_k}+1}
\rangle.
\]

Let \(I_{\rm geom}\) be the controlled-incidence ideal generated by the equations for

\[
M=0,\quad W=0,\quad K_v=0,\quad T_v=0,
\]

plus collision, endpoint-gap, patch-boundary, amplitude-drop, whitening singularity,

\[
c=0,\qquad A_5^{\mathfrak f}=0,
\]

and hidden-rank jump conditions.

Exact zero-anomaly control is the variety inclusion

\[
V(I_C)\subseteq V(I_{\rm geom}).
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\sqrt{I_{\rm geom}}\subseteq \sqrt{I_C}.
}
\]

This is the exact algebraic theorem needed to say:

\[
H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\theta\in\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

The current paper-state does not establish this radical containment.

---

# 2. Exact-zero control is still insufficient

Even if

\[
V(I_C)\subseteq V(I_{\rm geom})
\]

were proved, it would not imply the sampled lower bound.

A point can satisfy

\[
\theta\notin V(I_C)\cup V(I_{\rm geom})
\]

while

\[
0<\|C_{\rm fd}(\theta)\|_\infty\ll \Lambda(m,Q).
\]

Local model:

\[
I_C=\langle x\rangle,\qquad I_{\rm geom}=\langle x\rangle.
\]

Then exact containment is perfect:

\[
V(I_C)=V(I_{\rm geom}).
\]

But the points

\[
x=\varepsilon,\qquad 0<|\varepsilon|<\Lambda
\]

are outside both exact loci while violating radial anti-smallness.

Therefore the finite-core proof also needs a **collar exclusion**:

\[
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\operatorname{dist}(\theta(m),\mathcal E_{\rm geom})
\gtrsim \Lambda(m,Q)^{1/\mu}
\]

or directly

\[
\|C_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge \Lambda(m,Q).
\]

---

# 3. Łojasiewicz gives only a conditional bridge

If exact zero control holds, then Łojasiewicz gives a local inequality of the form

\[
\|C_{\rm fd}(\theta)\|_\infty
\ge
A\,
\operatorname{dist}(\theta,V(I_C))^\mu.
\]

If

\[
V(I_C)\subseteq \mathcal E_{\rm geom},
\]

then

\[
\operatorname{dist}(\theta,V(I_C))
\ge
\operatorname{dist}(\theta,\mathcal E_{\rm geom})
\]

up to local constants only on a stratified compact patch.

Thus one could get

\[
\|C_{\rm fd}(\theta)\|_\infty
\gtrsim
\operatorname{dist}(\theta,\mathcal E_{\rm geom})^\mu.
\]

But this helps only if actual zeta samples satisfy a calibrated incidence-collar separation:

\[
\operatorname{dist}(\theta(m),\mathcal E_{\rm geom})
\gtrsim
\Lambda(m,Q)^{1/\mu}.
\]

No such theorem is currently present.

So the correct implication stack is:

\[
\boxed{
V(I_C)\subseteq\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
}
\]

plus

\[
\boxed{
\text{sampled collar separation from }\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
}
\]

implies

\[
\boxed{
\text{radial sampled anti-smallness.}
}
\]

The current draft has neither of the first two.

---

# 4. Interaction vector makes radical containment doubtful

The finite vector is

\[
C_{\rm fd}
=
P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}.
\]

If \(J_{\rm fd}\) were absent or sign-controlled, one might hope that

\[
C_{\rm fd}=0
\]

forces one of the known degeneracies. But the current state explicitly keeps the interaction branch live. At first order,

\[
c_{\core,1}
=
\sum_\nu a_\nu K(d_\nu)+J_1.
\]

The source-level interaction \(J_1\) is not proved zero, sign-controlled, or incidence-controlled. The current instructions also emphasize that the full vector

\[
J_{\rm fd}=(J_1,J_3,\ldots,J_{2R+1})
\]

may cancel the pair-like vector. 

Thus the radical containment

\[
\sqrt{I_{\rm geom}}\subseteq \sqrt{I_C}
\]

is not just unproved; it is structurally suspect unless the paper adds a theorem controlling interaction directions.

A formal exact-zero model:

\[
P_{\rm fd}=P_0\neq0,
\qquad
J_{\rm fd}=-P_0.
\]

Then

\[
C_{\rm fd}=0
\]

while all controlled incidence variables can be kept nonzero. This gives

\[
\theta\in V(I_C)\setminus \mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\]

unless a source theorem forbids that interaction vector.

---

# 5. Necessary theorem: interaction ideal containment

The theorem needed for exact-zero control is:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Finite-core interaction ideal containment]
Let
\[
I_C
=
\langle
P_1+J_1,\,
P_3+J_3,\,
\ldots,\,
P_{2R_{\Theta_k}+1}+J_{2R_{\Theta_k}+1}
\rangle
\]
be the finite-core coefficient ideal on a compact nonsingular actual-source
\(k\)-core stratum. Let \(I_{\rm geom}\) be the controlled-incidence ideal.
Then
\[
V(I_C)\subseteq V(I_{\rm geom}),
\]
equivalently
\[
\sqrt{I_{\rm geom}}\subseteq \sqrt{I_C}.
\]
\end{theorem}
```

This would prove that exact zero-anomaly implies controlled incidence.

But it still would not prove calibrated non-concentration. For that, the stronger theorem is:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Calibrated finite-core interaction anti-cancellation]
For every actual zeta finite-core parameter
\[
\theta(m)\in\Theta_k\setminus\mathcal E_{\rm geom},
\]
one has
\[
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]
\end{theorem}
```

This is exactly the sampled coefficient non-concentration theorem in interaction form.

---

# 6. The sharpened bad branch

The unresolved branch should be stated as an interaction-cancellation small-value branch:

\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm vec}(m,Q)
=
\left\{
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal E_{\rm geom}:
0<
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
<
\Lambda(m,Q)
\right\}.
\]

This branch includes two subcases:

### Exact-interaction zero branch

\[
P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}=0,
\qquad
\theta\notin\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

This refutes exact zero-anomaly control.

### Near-interaction cancellation branch

\[
0<
\|P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}\|_\infty
<
\Lambda(m,Q),
\qquad
\theta\notin\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

This refutes calibrated radial anti-smallness even if exact zero-anomaly is controlled.

---

# 7. Current conclusion

The finite-core branch now has a precise algebraic-analytic decomposition:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Exact problem: }
V(I_C)\subseteq\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Calibrated problem: }
\|C_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty\ge\Lambda(m,Q).
}
\]

The first is an ideal-containment / interaction-rigidity theorem. The second is a pointwise sampled anti-cancellation theorem. Neither follows from current finite determinacy, compactness, zero-spacing, endpoint controls, or \(N\)-point positivity.

---

## Bottom line

The finite-core anti-smallness theorem is blocked by a concrete algebraic alternative:

\[
\boxed{
P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}
\text{ may vanish or become arbitrarily small outside }
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
}
\]

To close FC-A, the proof must add either:

\[
\boxed{
\sqrt{I_{\rm geom}}\subseteq \sqrt{I_C}
}
\]

plus a calibrated collar-exclusion theorem, or directly:

\[
\boxed{
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge\Lambda(m,Q).
}
\]

This is now the exact finite-core obstruction.

I’ll try a perturbative route: if finite-core interactions are uniformly dominated by the pair-like vector, radial anti-smallness would follow. ## Finite-Core A — continued attack via interaction dominance

### New route tested

A plausible way to prove radial sampled anti-smallness would be to show that interaction corrections are perturbatively dominated by the pair-like / one-body finite vector:

\[
C_{\rm fd}=P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd},
\]

with

\[
\|J_{\rm fd}\| \le \rho \|P_{\rm fd}\|,
\qquad
\rho<1.
\]

If this were true, then

\[
\|C_{\rm fd}\|
\ge
(1-\rho)\|P_{\rm fd}\|,
\]

and radial anti-smallness would reduce to a lower bound for \(P_{\rm fd}\), which is much more plausible because the pair-like piece has positivity structure.

But this route fails under the current proof architecture: **finite same-scale cores are not perturbative**. The interaction vector is not shown to be lower-order, small-norm, cone-contained, or sign-compatible. The current consolidated state explicitly says the interaction vector \(J_{\rm fd}\) can formally cancel the pair-like vector \(P_{\rm fd}\) and that no theorem currently rules this out. 

---

# 1. Perturbative domination would close the branch

Let

\[
C_{\rm fd}(\theta)
=
(c_{\core,1},c_{\core,3},\ldots,c_{\core,2R+1})(\theta)
=
P_{\rm fd}(\theta)+J_{\rm fd}(\theta).
\]

Suppose on a compact nonsingular stratum outside controlled incidence one had

\[
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta)\|_\infty
\ge P_0(m,Q)
\]

and

\[
\|J_{\rm fd}(\theta)\|_\infty
\le
\rho \|P_{\rm fd}(\theta)\|_\infty,
\qquad
\rho<1.
\]

Then

\[
\|C_{\rm fd}(\theta)\|_\infty
\ge
(1-\rho)P_0(m,Q).
\]

If

\[
P_0(m,Q)
\gtrsim
\Lambda(m,Q),
\]

where

\[
\Lambda(m,Q)
=
C_*
\max_{1\le N\le R+1}
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right),
\]

then sampled coefficient non-concentration follows.

So one sufficient theorem is:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Finite-core perturbative interaction domination]
On each compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum, outside
\(\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}\), the interaction vector satisfies
\[
\|J_{\rm fd}(\theta)\|_\infty
\le
\rho_{\Theta_k}\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta)\|_\infty,
\qquad
\rho_{\Theta_k}<1.
\]
\end{theorem}
```

This theorem would close the radial branch if the pair-like vector has the calibrated lower scale.

---

# 2. Why same-scale finite cores do not give perturbative domination

The problem is that the finite-core branch is explicitly **same-scale**. The constituents are not separated into a dominant pair plus negligible interactions. Interactions are of the same normalized order as pair-like terms.

At first order,

\[
c_{\core,1}
=
\sum_\nu a_\nu K(d_\nu)+J_1,
\]

where

\[
J_1=[s]\Phi_K(\mathcal I_{\ge2}).
\]

The pair-like sum may have positivity, but \(J_1\) is not shown to be small compared with it. In fact, the interaction branch remains independently live: the current state says \(J_1\) is not proved zero, sign-controlled, or incidence-controlled. 

So the estimate

\[
\|J_{\rm fd}\|\le \rho\|P_{\rm fd}\|
\]

has no support in the present framework.

---

# 3. Cone separation is the non-perturbative replacement

Since interactions need not be small, the next possible route is cone separation.

Suppose

\[
P_{\rm fd}(\theta)\in \mathcal C_P,
\qquad
J_{\rm fd}(\theta)\in \mathcal C_J,
\]

and the cones satisfy

\[
\operatorname{dist}(-\mathcal C_P,\mathcal C_J)>0
\]

after normalization. Then

\[
P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}
\]

cannot be small unless one of the vectors is small or a controlled incidence occurs.

A theorem-ready version:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Finite-core finite-vector cone separation]
On every compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum, outside
\(\mathcal E_{\rm geom}\), there exist closed cones
\(\mathcal C_P,\mathcal C_J\subset \mathbb C^{R_{\Theta_k}+1}\) such that
\[
P_{\rm fd}(\theta)\in\mathcal C_P,\qquad
J_{\rm fd}(\theta)\in\mathcal C_J,
\]
and
\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
-\mathcal C_P\cap S,\,
\mathcal C_J\cap S
\right)
\ge c_{\Theta_k}>0.
\]
Then
\[
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta)+J_{\rm fd}(\theta)\|_\infty
\ge
c_{\Theta_k}
\left(
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta)\|_\infty+\|J_{\rm fd}(\theta)\|_\infty
\right).
\]
\end{theorem}
```

But the paper currently has no such cone theorem for \(J_{\rm fd}\). The interaction data include transverse \(dd\)-fiber terms and centered-kernel spectral issues, and those remain uncontrolled. The latest consolidated state identifies exactly these interaction terms as live blockers. 

---

# 4. Formal obstruction to perturbative or cone closure

Let

\[
P_{\rm fd}=P_0\ne0.
\]

If the interaction space contains a direction arbitrarily close to

\[
-P_0,
\]

then for any small \(\varepsilon\),

\[
J_{\rm fd}= -P_0+\varepsilon v
\]

gives

\[
C_{\rm fd}
=
P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}
=
\varepsilon v.
\]

Then

\[
0<\|C_{\rm fd}\|_\infty<\Lambda(m,Q)
\]

for \(\varepsilon\) small, while

\[
\theta\notin\mathcal Z_k
\]

and all controlled incidence functions can remain nonzero.

So the exact obstruction is:

\[
\boxed{
-\frac{P_{\rm fd}}{\|P_{\rm fd}\|}
\in
\overline{
\left\{
\frac{J_{\rm fd}}{\|J_{\rm fd}\|}:
\theta\in\Theta_k\setminus\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\right\}
}.
}
\]

The current paper does not exclude this.

---

# 5. Relation to centered \(dd\)-kernel obstruction

The interaction blocker provides a concrete source for failure of cone separation.

Under the favorable separation-kernel reduction,

\[
\mathfrak j_{ij}^{dd}
=
K_{dd}(u_i-u_j;m),
\]

one still needs the centered kernel matrix to be one-sided on the balanced subspace. For \(k=3\), with

\[
u=(-1,0,1),
\]

the condition involves

\[
A=K_{dd}(1;m),
\qquad
B=K_{dd}(2;m),
\]

and requires a nontrivial inequality such as

\[
A\ge \frac14B
\]

under the relevant phase/sign convention. The current state says analyticity, evenness, collision divisibility, same-scale compactness, and pair-like positivity do not imply this. 

Therefore the \(dd\)-interaction can plausibly point against the pair-like finite vector and feed

\[
P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}\approx0.
\]

---

# 6. Sharpened missing theorem

The finite-core theorem now needed can be stated as finite-vector angle separation:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Finite-core pair-interaction angle separation]
Let
\[
C_{\rm fd}=P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}
\]
on a compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum.  For every actual
zeta finite-core parameter
\[
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom},
\]
the angle between \(P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\) and
\(-J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\) is bounded away from zero at the calibrated scale:
\[
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]
\end{theorem}
```

Equivalent sampled coefficient form:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Sampled coefficient non-concentration]
For every actual zeta finite-core parameter outside
\(\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}\),
\[
\max_N |F_N(\theta(m),Q)|\ge \Lambda(m,Q).
\]
\end{theorem}
```

These are the same finite-core requirement in different language.

---

# 7. Updated unresolved branch

The live branch is now best named as an **interaction-angle cancellation branch**:

\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm angle}(m,Q)
=
\left\{
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}:
0<
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
<
\Lambda(m,Q)
\right\}.
\]

This branch captures the mechanism more precisely than the generic coefficient-small branch.

---

## Bottom line

The perturbative route fails because same-scale finite cores do not make interactions small.

The cone-separation route would work, but the current draft does not prove the required cone or angle separation for

\[
J_{\rm fd}.
\]

Thus the finite-core obstruction is now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{interaction-angle cancellation}
}
\]

between

\[
P_{\rm fd}
\quad\text{and}\quad
J_{\rm fd}.
\]

To close it, the proof must prove perturbative domination, cone separation, centered-kernel spectral rigidity, or pointwise sampled coefficient non-concentration.

## Assistant (2026-04-25 12:54:19)

## Finite-Core A — continued attack via projective anti-alignment

### New reduction

The finite-core sampled non-concentration problem can be stated as a **finite-dimensional anti-alignment problem** between the pair-like vector and the interaction vector:

\[
C_{\rm fd}(\theta)
=
P_{\rm fd}(\theta)+J_{\rm fd}(\theta).
\]

The bad branch is precisely where

\[
J_{\rm fd}(\theta)
\approx
-P_{\rm fd}(\theta)
\]

at the calibrated scale. The current proof-state already identifies this finite-vector cancellation mechanism as live and not controlled by finite determinacy or projective detection. 

---

# 1. Projectivized anti-alignment criterion

Work on a compact nonsingular stratum and suppress the \(\theta\)-dependence. Assume first

\[
P_{\rm fd}\ne0.
\]

Set

\[
p=\frac{P_{\rm fd}}{\|P_{\rm fd}\|_\infty},
\qquad
j=\frac{J_{\rm fd}}{\|P_{\rm fd}\|_\infty}.
\]

Then

\[
C_{\rm fd}=P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}
\]

satisfies

\[
\|C_{\rm fd}\|_\infty
=
\|P_{\rm fd}\|_\infty
\|p+j\|_\infty.
\]

Thus sampled coefficient non-concentration follows from two independent inputs:

\[
\boxed{
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\gtrsim \Lambda(m,Q)
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\|p(\theta(m))+j(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge c_{\Theta_k}>0.
}
\]

The first is a pair-like radial lower bound. The second is projective anti-alignment exclusion.

The current draft has neither in this full finite-core setting.

---

# 2. Exact compactness criterion

Define the normalized anti-alignment set

\[
\mathcal A_k
=
\overline{
\left\{
\left(
\frac{P_{\rm fd}(\theta)}{\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta)\|_\infty},
\frac{J_{\rm fd}(\theta)}{\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta)\|_\infty}
\right):
\theta\in\Theta_k\setminus\mathcal E_{\rm geom},
\ P_{\rm fd}(\theta)\ne0
\right\}
}.
\]

Then a uniform anti-alignment gap is exactly the assertion that

\[
\mathcal A_k
\cap
\{(p,j):j=-p\}
=
\varnothing.
\]

If this intersection is empty, compactness gives

\[
\inf_{(p,j)\in\mathcal A_k}
\|p+j\|_\infty
=
c_{\Theta_k}>0.
\]

Then

\[
\|P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}\|_\infty
\ge
c_{\Theta_k}\|P_{\rm fd}\|_\infty.
\]

If the intersection is nonempty, then there are sequences outside controlled incidence with

\[
\frac{J_{\rm fd}}{\|P_{\rm fd}\|}
\to
-\frac{P_{\rm fd}}{\|P_{\rm fd}\|},
\]

and hence

\[
\|P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}\|_\infty
=o(\|P_{\rm fd}\|_\infty).
\]

So the anti-concentration theorem is equivalent to proving that actual zeta core samples avoid this anti-diagonal at calibrated scale.

---

# 3. Why current geometry does not give the gap

The current controlled incidence set includes

\[
M=0,\quad W=0,\quad K_v=0,\quad T_v=0,
\]

collision, endpoint-gap, patch-boundary, amplitude-drop, whitening singularity,

\[
c=0,\qquad A_5^{\mathfrak f}=0,
\]

and hidden-rank jumps.

These are scalar or low-dimensional geometric conditions. They do not currently control the **direction** of

\[
J_{\rm fd}
\]

inside

\[
\mathbb C^{R_{\Theta_k}+1}.
\]

In particular, the active interaction blocker contains transverse \(dd\)-fiber data and centered-kernel spectral freedom. The latest consolidation says these interactions are not proved zero, sign-controlled, or incidence-contained. 

Therefore the proof does not rule out

\[
J_{\rm fd}\approx -P_{\rm fd}
\]

outside controlled incidence.

---

# 4. Dimension/rank obstruction

Suppose the interaction map has local parameters \(\zeta\) and

\[
J_{\rm fd}=J_{\rm fd}(\zeta).
\]

If the differential

\[
D_\zeta J_{\rm fd}
\]

has image containing the line through

\[
-P_{\rm fd},
\]

then one can move \(J_{\rm fd}\) toward \(-P_{\rm fd}\) to first order.

If the image has enough rank to solve

\[
P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}=0,
\]

then exact zero-anomaly points outside \(\mathcal E_{\rm geom}\) are locally possible. If the rank is smaller, near-cancellation may still be possible unless the image cone is separated from \(-P_{\rm fd}\).

So a sufficient obstruction theorem would need to show:

\[
-P_{\rm fd}(\theta)
\notin
\overline{\operatorname{Cone}
\left(
J_{\rm fd}(\Theta_k\setminus\mathcal E_{\rm geom})
\right)}
\]

with a quantitative gap.

The draft has no such rank, cone, or image-separation theorem.

---

# 5. Formal anti-alignment model

Let

\[
P_{\rm fd}=P_0\ne0.
\]

Let the interaction vector have one scalar parameter \(t\):

\[
J_{\rm fd}(t)
=
-tP_0.
\]

All controlled incidence functions are fixed nonzero. Then

\[
C_{\rm fd}(t)
=
(1-t)P_0.
\]

For

\[
t=1-\varepsilon,
\qquad
0<|\varepsilon|<\frac{\Lambda(m,Q)}{\|P_0\|_\infty},
\]

one has

\[
0<
\|C_{\rm fd}(t)\|_\infty
<
\Lambda(m,Q),
\]

while

\[
\theta(t)\notin \mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

This formal model satisfies finite determinacy, projective detection, compactness, and noncollision assumptions. It violates only the desired anti-alignment theorem.

Thus the missing input is genuinely about the image of the actual interaction map, not about the \(N\)-point projector.

---

# 6. Sharper theorem needed

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Finite-core pair--interaction anti-alignment]
\label{thm:finite-core-pair-interaction-anti-alignment}
Let \(\Theta_k\) be a compact nonsingular normalized actual-source
\(k\)-core stratum.  Write
\[
C_{\rm fd}(\theta)=P_{\rm fd}(\theta)+J_{\rm fd}(\theta).
\]
There exists \(c_{\Theta_k}>0\) such that for every
\[
\theta\in\Theta_k\setminus\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\]
with \(P_{\rm fd}(\theta)\ne0\),
\[
\left\|
\frac{P_{\rm fd}(\theta)}{\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta)\|_\infty}
+
\frac{J_{\rm fd}(\theta)}{\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta)\|_\infty}
\right\|_\infty
\ge
c_{\Theta_k}.
\]
\end{theorem}
```

Together with a pair-like radial lower bound

\[
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\gtrsim
\Lambda(m,Q),
\]

this implies sampled coefficient non-concentration.

But the theorem is not proved by the current source geometry.

---

# 7. Equivalent sampled version

The above theorem can be merged into the direct sampled coefficient theorem:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Pointwise sampled finite-core coefficient non-concentration]
\label{thm:pointwise-sampled-finite-core-coefficient-nonconcentration}
For every actual zeta finite-core parameter
\[
\theta(m)\in\Theta_k\setminus(\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}),
\]
\[
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
|F_N(\theta(m),Q)|
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]
\end{theorem}
```

This remains the cleanest theorem for the global proof.

---

# 8. Updated bad branch

The unresolved finite-core branch is now best written as:

```latex
\begin{definition}[Pair--interaction anti-alignment branch]
\label{def:pair-interaction-anti-alignment-branch}
Let
\[
C_{\rm fd}=P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}.
\]
Define \(\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}(m,Q)\) to be the set of actual zeta
finite-core parameters
\[
\theta(m)\in\Theta_k\setminus(\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom})
\]
such that
\[
0<
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
<
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]
\end{definition}
```

This branch explicitly records the cancellation mechanism.

---

## Bottom line

The attack now shows that finite-core non-concentration is equivalent to proving **pair–interaction anti-alignment** at calibrated scale.

The current draft does not prove that

\[
J_{\rm fd}
\]

is small, sign-constrained, cone-separated, incidence-contained, or otherwise prevented from pointing toward

\[
-P_{\rm fd}.
\]

Thus the finite-core branch remains open as

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}(m,Q).
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-25 12:55:14)

I’ll now attack the assumption that the pair-like vector \(P_{\rm fd}\) itself has a calibrated lower bound. Even if interaction anti-alignment were solved, the proof still needs a pair-like finite-vector lower law for the actual sampled core.

## Finite-Core A — continued attack: pair-like vector lower bound

### New issue

The previous reduction showed that finite-core non-concentration would follow from two inputs:

\[
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty \gtrsim \Lambda(m,Q)
\]

and

\[
P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m)) + J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))
\not\approx 0.
\]

I attacked the second input as pair–interaction anti-alignment. Now the first input also needs scrutiny.

The current draft-state does **not** prove a calibrated lower bound for the pair-like finite vector

\[
P_{\rm fd}
\]

itself, except in the special pair-like asymptotic branch. The consolidated prompt explicitly distinguishes the finite-core blocker from the already-handled qualitative finite determinacy and identifies sampled coefficient non-concentration / radial anti-smallness as live. 

---

# 1. Pair-like positivity is not automatically finite-vector non-concentration

At first odd order, the pair-like contribution has schematic form

\[
P_1(\theta)
=
\sum_{\nu} a_\nu K(d_\nu),
\]

where \(K(d)\) has favorable positivity in the pure pair-like model.

If all amplitudes \(a_\nu\) were positive real weights and all \(K(d_\nu)\) lay in a common open half-plane with a uniform angle gap, then one would get

\[
|P_1(\theta)|
\ge
c\sum_\nu |a_\nu||K(d_\nu)|.
\]

But the finite-core source model is not merely a positive sum of isolated pair-like pieces. It includes balanced source weights, mixed interactions, and higher coefficient channels. The current proof-state does not give a theorem that the full vector

\[
P_{\rm fd}
=
(P_1,P_3,\ldots,P_{2R+1})
\]

is uniformly separated from zero outside controlled incidence.

So even before adding

\[
J_{\rm fd},
\]

one needs a lower theorem for

\[
P_{\rm fd}.
\]

---

# 2. Pair-like scalar positivity does not imply vector lower bound

Suppose each one-pair contribution gives a vector

\[
V(d)
=
(K_1(d),K_3(d),\ldots,K_{2R+1}(d))
\in\mathbb C^{R+1}.
\]

Then

\[
P_{\rm fd}
=
\sum_\nu a_\nu V(d_\nu).
\]

A scalar theorem like

\[
\Re K_1(d)>0
\]

does not prevent the full vector sum from being small if the amplitudes are signed or balanced, or if different \(V(d_\nu)\) point in different directions in \(\mathbb C^{R+1}\).

A formal example:

\[
V(d_1)=(1,0),\qquad
V(d_2)=(1,\varepsilon),
\]

with weights

\[
a_1=1,\qquad a_2=-1.
\]

Then

\[
P_{\rm fd}
=
(0,-\varepsilon),
\]

which is arbitrarily small although neither one-pair vector is zero.

This is not claiming the zeta source realizes this exact example. It shows the required conclusion is not a formal consequence of one-pair positivity.

---

# 3. What theorem would give the pair-like lower law?

A sufficient theorem would be a finite-vector Chebyshev/full-spark lower bound:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Pair-like finite-vector lower law]
Let \(V(d)=(K_1(d),K_3(d),\ldots,K_{2R+1}(d))\) be the pair-like
finite-vector contribution on a compact same-scale patch.  For every
admissible finite source configuration outside controlled incidence,
\[
P_{\rm fd}(\theta)
=
\sum_\nu a_\nu V(d_\nu)
\]
satisfies
\[
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta)\|_\infty
\ge
c_{\Theta_k}\,\mathcal A(\theta),
\]
where \(\mathcal A(\theta)\) is the normalized source-amplitude scale.
\]
\end{theorem}
```

To make this useful for the global proof, one also needs

\[
\mathcal A(\theta(m))\gtrsim \Lambda(m,Q).
\]

This theorem is not presently established for the general finite-core branch.

---

# 4. ECT could be relevant, but only if it applies to the actual finite-vector family

An extended complete Chebyshev / full-spark theorem could rule out cancellations of

\[
\sum_\nu a_\nu V(d_\nu)
\]

under constraints on the number of nodes, signs, and amplitudes. But the theorem would need to apply to the **actual vector family**

\[
V(d)=
(K_1(d),K_3(d),\ldots,K_{2R+1}(d)),
\]

with the actual source weights and the actual same-scale normalization.

A generic ECT statement about a lower-order defect-free curve is not enough unless it proves:

\[
\sum_\nu a_\nu V(d_\nu)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\theta\in\mathcal E_{\rm geom},
\]

and a calibrated near-zero version

\[
0<\left\|\sum_\nu a_\nu V(d_\nu)\right\|_\infty<\Lambda(m,Q)
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\theta\in\text{controlled collar}.
\]

That theorem is not currently available.

---

# 5. The finite-core theorem stack is now three-layered

The sampled non-concentration theorem decomposes into:

### A. Pair-like finite-vector lower law

\[
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\gtrsim \Lambda(m,Q)
\]

outside pair-like controlled incidences.

### B. Interaction anti-alignment

\[
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\gtrsim
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty.
\]

### C. Sampled/collar exclusion

Even if exact zero sets are controlled, actual samples must not approach those sets closer than the calibrated scale.

The current draft-state does not prove A, B, or C in the full finite-core setting.

---

# 6. Formal branch showing pair-like lower failure

Define a compact finite-core patch with two nondegenerate pair-like constituents and no interaction:

\[
J_{\rm fd}=0.
\]

Let

\[
P_{\rm fd}(\varepsilon)
=
\varepsilon e_1,
\qquad
0<|\varepsilon|<\Lambda(m,Q).
\]

All controlled incidence variables can be fixed away from zero. Finite determinacy holds because

\[
P_{\rm fd}(\varepsilon)=0
\]

only at \(\varepsilon=0\), but for nonzero small \(\varepsilon\)

\[
0<\|P_{\rm fd}\|_\infty<\Lambda(m,Q).
\]

So even without interactions, radial anti-smallness is not formal. It needs a pair-like finite-vector anti-cancellation theorem or a sampled separation theorem.

---

# 7. Refined missing theorem

The cleanest global theorem remains sampled coefficient non-concentration:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Pointwise sampled finite-core coefficient non-concentration]
For every actual zeta finite-core parameter
\[
\theta(m)\in\Theta_k\setminus(\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}),
\]
one has
\[
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
|F_N(\theta(m),Q)|
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]
\end{theorem}
```

But internally this theorem requires at least one of:

\[
\boxed{
\text{pair-like finite-vector lower law + interaction anti-alignment,}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{direct arithmetic sampled separation of }C_{\rm fd}.}
}
\]

---

# 8. Updated bad branch

The unresolved branch should allow both pair-like and interaction mechanisms:

\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm coef}(m,Q)
=
\left\{
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}:
0<
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
<
\Lambda(m,Q)
\right\}.
\]

Subbranches:

\[
\mathcal N_k^{P}
=
\{0<\|P_{\rm fd}\|<\Lambda\},
\]

\[
\mathcal N_k^{PJ}
=
\{\|P_{\rm fd}\|\gtrsim\Lambda,\,
P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}\approx0\}.
\]

The first is pair-like finite-vector smallness. The second is interaction anti-alignment.

---

## Bottom line

The finite-core blocker is even sharper:

\[
\boxed{
\text{sampled coefficient non-concentration requires both}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{pair-like finite-vector lower bounds}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\text{interaction anti-alignment.}
}
\]

The current proof-state does not establish either for general finite same-scale cores.

## Finite-Core A — theorem-dependency block

The finite-core branch should now be treated as a **formal dependency**, not as another local coefficient-audit problem. The live dependency is exactly:

\[
\boxed{
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q)
}
\]

outside

\[
\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

This matches the current consolidated state: finite determinacy and projective detection are essentially done, while sampled/radial coefficient non-concentration remains open. 

---

# 1. Definitions

Let \(\Theta_k\) be a compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum.

Define the finite-determinacy coefficient vector

\[
C_{\rm fd}(\theta)
=
(c_{\core,1}(\theta),c_{\core,3}(\theta),\ldots,c_{\core,2R_{\Theta_k}+1}(\theta)).
\]

Decompose it as

\[
C_{\rm fd}(\theta)
=
P_{\rm fd}(\theta)+J_{\rm fd}(\theta),
\]

where \(P_{\rm fd}\) is the pair-like / one-body finite vector and \(J_{\rm fd}\) is the finite interaction vector

\[
J_{\rm fd}
=
(J_1,J_3,\ldots,J_{2R_{\Theta_k}+1}).
\]

Let

\[
\|H_{\core,\theta}\|_{\rm fd}
:=
\|C_{\rm fd}(\theta)\|_\infty.
\]

Let

\[
\mathcal Z_k
=
\{\theta:H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0\}
=
\{C_{\rm fd}(\theta)=0\}.
\]

For

\[
1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1,
\]

define the filtered coefficient

\[
F_N(\theta,Q)
=
c_{\core,2N-1}(\theta)
+
\sum_{j\ge1}
c_{\core,2N-1+2j}(\theta)
h_j(1^2,\dots,N^2)Q^{-2j}.
\]

The required sampled scale is

\[
\Lambda(m,Q)
:=
C_*
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right).
\]

---

# 2. Exact finite-core dependency

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Finite-core sampled non-concentration dependency]
\label{thm:finite-core-sampled-nonconcentration-dependency}
Let \(\Theta_k\) be a compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum.
Assume that every actual zeta finite-core parameter
\[
\theta(m)\in\Theta_k\setminus(\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom})
\]
satisfies
\[
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]
Then there exists an admissible bounded depth
\[
1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1
\]
such that
\[
|\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}(m)|
\ge
c_{\Theta_k}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m).
\]
\end{theorem}
```

---

# 3. Proof of dependency

Choose

\[
N_*
\in\{1,\ldots,R_{\Theta_k}+1\}
\]

such that

\[
|c_{\core,2N_*-1}(\theta(m))|
=
\|C_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty.
\]

Since

\[
C_{\rm fd}=P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd},
\]

the dependency assumption gives

\[
|c_{\core,2N_*-1}(\theta(m))|
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]

For \(Q\ge Q_0(\Theta_k)\), bounded-depth tail control gives

\[
|F_{N_*}(\theta(m),Q)-c_{\core,2N_*-1}(\theta(m))|
\le
\frac12
\|C_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty.
\]

Hence

\[
|F_{N_*}(\theta(m),Q)|
\ge
\frac12
\|C_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\frac12\Lambda(m,Q).
\]

The \(N\)-point scalar satisfies

\[
\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}
=
(-1)^{N+1}
(2N-1)N!(N-1)!
Q^{-(2N+2)}
F_N(\theta,Q).
\]

Therefore

\[
|\Xi_{\core}^{(N_*)}(m)|
\ge
\frac12
(2N_*-1)N_*!(N_*-1)!
Q^{-(2N_*+2)}
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]

By definition of \(\Lambda(m,Q)\),

\[
\Lambda(m,Q)
\ge
C_*
\frac{Q^{2N_*+2}}
{(2N_*-1)N_*!(N_*-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m).
\]

Substitution gives

\[
|\Xi_{\core}^{(N_*)}(m)|
\ge
\frac{C_*}{2}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m).
\]

Thus finite-core lower transfer follows.

---

# 4. Exact bad branch

If the dependency is not proved, the unresolved finite-core branch is:

```latex
\begin{definition}[Finite-core alignment-small branch]
\label{def:finite-core-alignment-small-branch}
Let
\[
C_{\rm fd}=P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}.
\]
Define
\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}(m,Q)
\]
to be the set of actual zeta finite-core parameters
\[
\theta(m)\in\Theta_k\setminus(\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom})
\]
such that
\[
0<
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
<
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]
\end{definition}
```

This branch is exactly equivalent, up to the already-handled \(Q^{-2}\)-tail error, to the coefficient-small branch

\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm coef}(m,Q)
=
\left\{
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}:
\max_N |F_N(\theta(m),Q)|<\Lambda(m,Q)
\right\}.
\]

---

# 5. Minimal missing input

The missing theorem is not finite determinacy and not projective detection. It is:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Finite-vector sampled anti-cancellation]
\label{thm:finite-vector-sampled-anticancellation}
For every actual zeta finite-core parameter
\[
\theta(m)\in\Theta_k\setminus(\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}),
\]
one has
\[
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]
\end{theorem}
```

Equivalently, one of the following must be proved:

\[
\boxed{
\text{pair-like finite-vector lower law}
+
\text{interaction anti-alignment}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{direct arithmetic sampled coefficient non-concentration}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{source-level anti-cancellation forcing }
P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}\text{ small into }\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
}
\]

None of these is currently supplied by the draft state.

---

## Bottom line

The finite-core dependency is now exact:

\[
\boxed{
\|P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}\|_\infty\ge\Lambda(m,Q)
\Longrightarrow
\exists N:\ |\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}|
\gtrsim
\frac{x}{B_\zeta}S.
}
\]

The remaining missing input is the pointwise finite-vector anti-cancellation theorem. Without it, the proof must carry the live branch

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}(m,Q).
}
\]

## Finite-core dependency-writing agent

### Output

The finite-core branch should now be recorded as a **formal conditional dependency**, not as a coefficient-hunting target.

The missing dependency is:

\[
\boxed{
\theta(m)\notin \mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge \Lambda(m,Q).
}
\]

If this theorem is assumed, finite-core lower transfer follows cleanly from finite determinacy, bounded \(N\)-point projective detection, and \(Q^{-2}\)-tail control. The latest consolidation states this is exactly the finite-core branch status and recommends treating it as a named dependency. 

---

# 1. Definitions

Let \(\Theta_k\) be a compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum.

Define the finite-determinacy coefficient vector

\[
C_{\rm fd}(\theta)
=
\left(
c_{\core,1}(\theta),
c_{\core,3}(\theta),
\ldots,
c_{\core,2R_{\Theta_k}+1}(\theta)
\right).
\]

Decompose it as

\[
C_{\rm fd}(\theta)
=
P_{\rm fd}(\theta)+J_{\rm fd}(\theta),
\]

where \(P_{\rm fd}\) is the pair-like / one-body contribution and

\[
J_{\rm fd}
=
(J_1,J_3,\ldots,J_{2R_{\Theta_k}+1})
\]

is the finite interaction vector.

Define

\[
\mathcal Z_k
=
\{\theta:H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0\}
=
\{C_{\rm fd}(\theta)=0\}.
\]

Define the finite-determinacy norm

\[
\|H_{\core,\theta}\|_{\rm fd}
:=
\|C_{\rm fd}(\theta)\|_\infty.
\]

For \(1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1\), set

\[
F_N(\theta,Q)
=
c_{\core,2N-1}(\theta)
+
\sum_{j\ge1}
c_{\core,2N-1+2j}(\theta)
h_j(1^2,\ldots,N^2)Q^{-2j}.
\]

Let

\[
\Lambda(m,Q)
=
C_*
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right).
\]

---

# 2. Named dependency

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Finite-core sampled vector non-concentration dependency]
\label{thm:finite-core-sampled-vector-nonconcentration}
Let \(\Theta_k\) be a compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum.
For every actual zeta finite-core parameter
\[
\theta(m)\in \Theta_k\setminus(\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}),
\]
assume
\[
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]
Then there exists an admissible bounded depth
\[
1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1
\]
such that
\[
|\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}(m)|
\ge
c_{\Theta_k}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m).
\]
\end{theorem}
```

---

# 3. Proof of implication

Since

\[
C_{\rm fd}=P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd},
\]

the hypothesis gives

\[
\|C_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]

Choose \(N_*\) such that

\[
|c_{\core,2N_*-1}(\theta(m))|
=
\|C_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty.
\]

For \(Q\ge Q_0(\Theta_k)\), bounded-depth tail control gives

\[
|F_{N_*}(\theta(m),Q)
-
c_{\core,2N_*-1}(\theta(m))|
\le
\frac12
\|C_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty.
\]

Therefore

\[
|F_{N_*}(\theta(m),Q)|
\ge
\frac12
\|C_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\frac12\Lambda(m,Q).
\]

The \(N\)-point scalar is

\[
\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}
=
(-1)^{N+1}
(2N-1)N!(N-1)!
Q^{-(2N+2)}
F_N(\theta,Q).
\]

Hence

\[
|\Xi_{\core}^{(N_*)}(m)|
\ge
\frac12
(2N_*-1)N_*!(N_*-1)!
Q^{-(2N_*+2)}
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]

By definition of \(\Lambda(m,Q)\),

\[
\Lambda(m,Q)
\ge
C_*
\frac{Q^{2N_*+2}}
{(2N_*-1)N_*!(N_*-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m).
\]

Substituting,

\[
|\Xi_{\core}^{(N_*)}(m)|
\ge
\frac{C_*}{2}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m).
\]

Thus

\[
c_{\Theta_k}=\frac{C_*}{2}
\]

is admissible, up to the fixed constants hidden in the tail-control and norm-comparison estimates.

---

# 4. Exact bad branch if the dependency is not assumed

```latex
\begin{definition}[Finite-core alignment-small branch]
\label{def:finite-core-alignment-small-branch}
Let
\[
C_{\rm fd}=P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}.
\]
Define
\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}(m,Q)
\]
to be the set of actual zeta finite-core parameters
\[
\theta(m)\in\Theta_k\setminus(\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom})

\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty

\Lambda(m,Q).
```

This is equivalent, up to the already-handled bounded-depth \(Q^{-2}\)-tail estimate, to the coefficient-small branch

\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm coef}(m,Q)
=
\left\{
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}:
\max_N |F_N(\theta(m),Q)|<\Lambda(m,Q)
\right\}.
\]

---

# 5. Minimal missing input

The missing theorem is:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Finite-vector sampled anti-cancellation]
\label{thm:finite-vector-sampled-anticancellation}
For every actual zeta finite-core parameter
\[
\theta(m)\in\Theta_k\setminus(\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}),
\]
one has
\[
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]
\end{theorem}
```

Equivalently, one must prove at least one of:

\[
\boxed{
\text{pair-like finite-vector lower law}
+
\text{interaction anti-alignment}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{direct pointwise sampled coefficient non-concentration}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{source-level anti-cancellation forcing }
P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}\text{ small into }\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
}
\]

---

## Bottom line

The finite-core proof dependency is now exact:

\[
\boxed{
\|P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}\|_\infty\ge\Lambda(m,Q)
}
\]

outside

\[
\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

Assuming it gives the required bounded-\(N\) lower transfer. Without it, the proof must carry the live branch

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}(m,Q).
}
\]
