## Assistant (2026-04-25 15:53:09)

_Thought for 27s_

## Finite-Core A — continued attack: analytic small-value exclusion

### Result

The sampled vector non-concentration theorem is stronger than “finite-core lower transfer.” It implies a **uniform small-value exclusion for analytic functions of normalized zeta core parameters**. The current draft does not contain such a theorem.

The live finite-core dependency remains:

\[
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]

The attached prompt identifies this as the sharp finite-core branch and explicitly says finite determinacy, compactness, pairwise zero spacing, endpoint gaps, discreteness, and Remez--Łojasiewicz volume estimates do not prove it. 

---

# 1. Reformulation as analytic small-value avoidance

Let

\[
G_N(\theta,Q):=F_N(\theta,Q)
\]

for

\[
1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1.
\]

The finite-core theorem requires

\[
\max_N |G_N(\theta(m),Q)|
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q)
\]

outside

\[
\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

So for the finite family of analytic functions

\[
\mathcal G_{\Theta_k,Q}
=
\{G_1,\ldots,G_{R_{\Theta_k}+1}\},
\]

the actual zeta sample set

\[
\Theta_k^{\zeta}
=
\{\theta(m):m \text{ is an actual finite-core midpoint}\}
\]

must avoid the analytic small-value tube

\[
\mathcal T_{\Lambda}
=
\left\{
\theta\in\Theta_k:
\theta\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom},
\quad
\max_N |G_N(\theta,Q)|<\Lambda(m,Q)
\right\}.
\]

That is a **pointwise avoidance theorem** for actual zeta samples.

This is not implied by saying that \(\mathcal T_\Lambda\) is small in volume or thin near \(\mathcal Z_k\).

---

# 2. Why zero-spacing cannot imply it

Zero-spacing gives lower bounds against equations like

\[
u_i=u_j.
\]

But the functions \(G_N\) define general analytic cancellation hypersurfaces.

A minimal model:

\[
G(u_1,u_2,u_3)=u_1+u_2-2u_3.
\]

The condition

\[
|u_i-u_j|\ge c>0
\]

does not prevent

\[
|G(u_1,u_2,u_3)|\ll 1.
\]

For example,

\[
u_1=0,\qquad u_2=2,\qquad u_3=1+\varepsilon
\]

has separated points but

\[
G=-2\varepsilon.
\]

Thus any theorem implying

\[
|G(\theta(m))|\ge\Lambda(m,Q)
\]

is not a spacing theorem. It is an **approximate-relation avoidance theorem**.

The finite-core functions \(F_N\) are exactly of this cancellation type, because

\[
C_{\rm fd}=P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}
\]

can be small through interaction alignment

\[
J_{\rm fd}\approx -P_{\rm fd}
\]

without collision or endpoint degeneration. 

---

# 3. Strong consequence: approximate finite-core relations must be forbidden

The sampled non-concentration theorem would imply that actual zeta finite cores avoid all approximate relations

\[
P_{\rm fd}(\theta)+J_{\rm fd}(\theta)
\approx0
\]

at scale

\[
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]

Equivalently, for every actual core,

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m)),
-P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))
\right)
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q)
\]

unless

\[
\theta(m)\in\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

This is stronger than any currently listed local geometric condition. The controlled data

\[
M,W,K_v,T_v
\]

do not determine the transverse Gram-state information feeding \(J_{\rm fd}\), and the interaction branch remains live through the \(dd\)-feature / spectral obstruction. 

---

# 4. Density estimates are structurally insufficient

Suppose one had a sublevel-volume estimate

\[
\operatorname{vol}
\left(
\theta\in\Theta_k:
\max_N |F_N(\theta,Q)|<\epsilon
\right)
\ll
\epsilon^\alpha.
\]

This does not imply pointwise exclusion of actual samples. To use it, one would need an effective distribution theorem:

\[
\#\{m\le T:\theta(m)\in \mathcal T_\epsilon\}
\le
C\epsilon^\alpha N(T)+E(T,\epsilon).
\]

For the RH proof, this would only help if

\[
C\epsilon^\alpha N(T)+E(T,\epsilon)<1
\]

at

\[
\epsilon=\Lambda(m,Q).
\]

The current proof has no such equidistribution theorem, and the proof needs to eliminate every bad finite core, not merely show such cores have density zero.

So a density result is not enough unless it is strong enough to become a **zero-count** result at the calibrated scale.

---

# 5. The exact missing theorem is a small-value avoidance theorem

The finite-core dependency should be stated as follows.

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Pointwise sampled finite-core small-value avoidance]
\label{thm:pointwise-sampled-finite-core-small-value-avoidance}
Let \(\Theta_k\) be a compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum.
For
\[
1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1
\]
set
\[
F_N(\theta,Q)
=
c_{\core,2N-1}(\theta)
+
\sum_{j\ge1}
c_{\core,2N-1+2j}(\theta)
h_j(1^2,\ldots,N^2)Q^{-2j}.
\]
Then every actual zeta finite-core parameter \(\theta(m)\in\Theta_k\) satisfies
one of the following:
\[
\theta(m)\in\mathcal Z_k,
\]
\[
\theta(m)\in\mathcal E_{\rm geom},
\]
or
\[
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
|F_N(\theta(m),Q)|
\ge
C_*
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right).
\]
\end{theorem}
```

Equivalently, in vector form:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Pointwise pair--interaction anti-alignment]
\label{thm:pointwise-pair-interaction-anti-alignment}
Let
\[
C_{\rm fd}=P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}.
\]
For every actual zeta finite-core parameter
\[
\theta(m)\in\Theta_k\setminus(\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}),
\]
one has
\[
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]
\end{theorem}
```

This is not currently proved.

---

# 6. Formal countermodel under current controls

The present controlled conditions allow the following finite-dimensional model.

Let all controlled incidence functions be bounded away from zero. Fix

\[
P_{\rm fd}=P_0\ne0.
\]

Let the interaction vector vary through

\[
J_{\rm fd}(t)=-P_0+t v,
\]

with

\[
v\ne0.
\]

Then

\[
C_{\rm fd}(t)=P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}(t)=t v.
\]

For

\[
0<|t|<\Lambda(m,Q)/\|v\|_\infty,
\]

one has

\[
0<\|C_{\rm fd}(t)\|_\infty<\Lambda(m,Q),
\]

while the point remains outside

\[
\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

This model violates only the desired sampled non-concentration theorem. It does not violate finite determinacy, projective detection, compactness, zero-spacing, endpoint-gap regularity, or \(N\)-point positivity.

Therefore the missing input is not a bookkeeping lemma. It is a genuine arithmetic/source-geometry separation theorem.

---

# 7. The bad branch to carry forward

```latex
\begin{definition}[Sampled coefficient-small finite-core branch]
\label{def:sampled-coefficient-small-finite-core-branch}
Let
\[
\Lambda(m,Q)
=
C_*
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right).
\]
Define
\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}(m,Q)
\]
to be the set of actual zeta finite-core parameters
\[
\theta(m)\in\Theta_k\setminus(\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom})
\]
such that
\[
0<
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
<
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]
\end{definition}
```

This is the exact unresolved finite-core branch.

---

## Bottom line

Finite-Core A cannot prove sampled vector non-concentration from the current framework.

The theorem needed is a **pointwise analytic small-value avoidance theorem** for actual zeta core samples:

\[
\boxed{
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\Rightarrow
\max_N |F_N(\theta(m),Q)|\ge\Lambda(m,Q).
}
\]

Equivalently:

\[
\boxed{
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge\Lambda(m,Q).
}
\]

No combination of finite determinacy, projective detection, zero-spacing, endpoint gaps, compactness, discreteness, or sublevel-volume estimates supplies this pointwise exclusion.

## Finite-Core Agent A — pointwise small-value avoidance audit

### Verdict

I do **not** find a proved draft theorem that gives the required pointwise sampled non-concentration:

\[
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]

The branch remains live as a formal dependency. The current handover also frames this as the exact finite-core blocker: finite determinacy and projective detection are done, while the missing input is pointwise sampled non-concentration / anti-alignment. 

---

# 1. Definitions reconstructed

The finite-determinacy vector is

\[
C_{\rm fd}(\theta)
=
(c_{\core,1}(\theta),c_{\core,3}(\theta),\ldots,c_{\core,2R_{\Theta_k}+1}(\theta)).
\]

The current decomposition is

\[
C_{\rm fd}(\theta)=P_{\rm fd}(\theta)+J_{\rm fd}(\theta),
\]

where \(P_{\rm fd}\) is the pair-like / one-body finite vector and \(J_{\rm fd}\) is the finite interaction vector.

For

\[
1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1,
\]

the filtered coefficient is

\[
F_N(\theta,Q)
=
c_{\core,2N-1}(\theta)
+
\sum_{j\ge1}
c_{\core,2N-1+2j}(\theta)
h_j(1^2,\ldots,N^2)Q^{-2j}.
\]

The calibrated target scale is

\[
\Lambda(m,Q)
=
C_*
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right).
\]

The missing theorem is equivalently

\[
\max_N |F_N(\theta(m),Q)|\ge \Lambda(m,Q)
\]

outside

\[
\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

---

# 2. What the current tools prove — and what they do not

### Compactness

Compactness gives uniform constants on \(\Theta_k\). It supports finite determinacy, norm comparison, and tail-control constants. It does **not** prevent an actual sampled point from lying in a thin analytic small-value tube.

### Finite determinacy

Finite determinacy gives

\[
C_{\rm fd}(\theta)=0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0
\]

on the relevant compact nonsingular stratum. It does **not** give a lower bound for nonzero

\[
\|C_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty.
\]

### Projective detection

For \(Q\) large enough, bounded-depth projective detection gives

\[
\max_N |F_N(\theta,Q)|
\asymp
\|C_{\rm fd}(\theta)\|_\infty.
\]

This reduces the problem to radial size. It does **not** prove that the radial size is at least \(\Lambda(m,Q)\).

### Zero-spacing / endpoint-gap control

These exclude collision or boundary degeneracy. They do not exclude analytic cancellation relations such as

\[
P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}\approx0.
\]

Spacing controls where points are; it does not lower-bound arbitrary analytic functions of the normalized core data.

### Łojasiewicz / Remez / sublevel estimates

These give geometric or measure-type estimates for small-value sets. They do not give pointwise exclusion of actual zeta samples unless paired with an equidistribution or Diophantine separation theorem strong enough to show that the number of bad samples is zero at scale \(\Lambda(m,Q)\).

No such pointwise sampling theorem appears in the current proof state.

---

# 3. Formal good-patch model showing the gap

The present controls allow the following finite-dimensional model.

Fix all controlled incidence quantities away from zero:

\[
M,W,K_v,T_v\neq0,
\]

with no collision, endpoint-gap failure, patch-boundary issue, amplitude drop, whitening singularity, \(c=0\), \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}=0\), or hidden-rank jump.

Let

\[
P_{\rm fd}=P_0\neq0
\]

and let the interaction vector vary as

\[
J_{\rm fd}(t)=-P_0+t\,v
\]

for some nonzero vector \(v\). Then

\[
C_{\rm fd}(t)=P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}(t)=t\,v.
\]

For

\[
0<|t|<\frac{\Lambda(m,Q)}{\|v\|_\infty},
\]

we have

\[
0<\|P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}\|_\infty<\Lambda(m,Q),
\]

while the sample remains outside

\[
\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

This model violates only the desired pointwise anti-alignment theorem. It does not violate finite determinacy, compactness, projective detection, zero-spacing, or endpoint-gap control.

---

# 4. Exact unresolved branch

```latex
\begin{definition}[Finite-core alignment-small branch]
\label{def:finite-core-alignment-small-branch}
Let
\[
C_{\rm fd}=P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}.
\]
Define
\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}(m,Q)
\]
to be the set of actual zeta finite-core parameters
\[
\theta(m)\in\Theta_k\setminus(\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom})
\]
such that
\[
0<
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
<
\Lambda(m,Q),
\]
where
\[
\Lambda(m,Q)
=
C_*
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right).
\]
\end{definition}
```

---

# 5. Exact missing theorem

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Pointwise sampled finite-core vector non-concentration]
\label{thm:pointwise-sampled-finite-core-vector-nonconcentration}
Let \(\Theta_k\) be a compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum.
For every actual zeta finite-core parameter
\[
\theta(m)\in\Theta_k\setminus(\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}),
\]
one has
\[
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]
\end{theorem}
```

Equivalently,

\[
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
|F_N(\theta(m),Q)|
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]

---

## Bottom line

Finite-Core Agent A cannot prove the pointwise small-value avoidance theorem from the current draft machinery.

The exact live branch is

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}(m,Q).
}
\]

To eliminate it, the proof needs a new pointwise arithmetic/source-geometry theorem preventing

\[
J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\approx -P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))
\]

at the calibrated scale outside controlled incidence.
